23:807:64696:17:16:72:540:511:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:and  there  is  no  way  to  reduce  the  losses  from  transport  costs.   Therefore,  distortions  arise  only
23:808:64808:16:17:72:540:495:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:when consumers purchase a good which is not optimal given their type - in particular, when High
23:809:64903:17:16:72:359:478:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:types do not purchase goodEbecause they are uninformed.
23:810:64958:16:16:88:539:462:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:A:Appendix  A  derives  the  socially-optimal  level  of  information  provisionθ+and  shows  that  it
23:811:65058:16:17:72:540:446:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:could  be  greater  than,  less  than,  or  equal  to  the  market  equilibrium  level.   The  market  is  more
23:812:65169:17:16:72:539:429:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:likely  to  under-provide  information  when  the  social  gainGHE−GIfrom  moving  consumers  to
23:813:65265:16:17:72:305:413:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:goodEis large or when market powertis small.
23:814:65309:17:16:88:539:396:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:A:We assume that the government cannot directly mandate sales agents or firms to achieveθ+,
23:815:65398:16:17:72:540:380:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:which  seems  realistic  in  most  contexts.   Instead,  consider  a  government  that  has  two  potential
23:816:65505:17:16:72:539:363:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:policy instruments:  a minimum quality standard or a sales incentive for goodEprovided directly
23:817:65600:16:32:71:309:347:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:to the agent.9What are the welfare implications?
23:818:65648:32:23:71:373:315:11:g_d0_f12:11:g_d0_f12:C:4.4.1    Welfare Effects of a Minimum Quality Standard
23:819:65702:23:17:71:539:292:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:As discussed in the introduction, minimum energy efficiency standards are often justified by the
23:820:65798:17:16:71:539:275:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:assertion  that  imperfect  information  reduces  demand  for  energy  efficient  goods.   In  this  model,
23:821:65905:16:17:71:539:259:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:one  can  capture  the  effects  of  a  minimum  quality  standard  by  eliminating  the  base  good  and
23:822:66010:17:16:71:539:242:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:requiring that all consumers purchase goodE.  Under our assumptions aboutGHE, GLE, andGI,
23:823:66099:16:16:72:540:226:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:this increases welfare for High type consumers but decreases welfare for Low types.  A minimum
23:824:66193:16:17:72:540:210:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:quality standard also eliminates information provision costs, as all consumers now are mandated
23:825:66288:17:16:72:426:193:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:to purchase goodE.  Under a minimum quality standard, social welfare is:
23:826:66360:16:15:84:540:177:6:g_d0_f5:9:g_d0_f6:F:9Our model is not well-suited to consider a subsidy for goodE.  In our model, a subsidy for goodEis equivalent
23:827:66470:15:11:71:540:162:9:g_d0_f6:9:g_d0_f6:F:to an equal reduction in marginal cost for both firms.  As long as the subsidized price still exceedsp∗fI, firms pass
23:828:66587:11:10:71:539:151:9:g_d0_f6:9:g_d0_f6:F:the subsidy on to consumers in the form of reduced prices, but because the price reduction is symmetric, there is no
23:829:66703:10:11:71:539:141:9:g_d0_f6:9:g_d0_f6:F:change inθ∗.  Thus, no additional consumers are informed, and the market equilibrium is unaffected except for the
23:830:66816:11:11:71:539:130:9:g_d0_f6:9:g_d0_f6:F:transfer from taxpayers to the government to firms to some High types.  This result would be different if we had a
23:831:66930:11:11:71:540:119:9:g_d0_f6:9:g_d0_f6:F:continuum of quality preferences instead of just binaryHandLtypes.  Note that in Propositions 1 and 3 and in our
23:832:67042:11:0:71:421:108:9:g_d0_f6:9:g_d0_f6:F:experiment, only one firm reduces prices, so ̃θfandqfEdo respond to changes inpfE.
24:833:67126:0:0:212:388:674:11:g_d0_f10:11:g_d0_f8:?:SWstandard=λGHE+ (1−λ)GLE−
24:834:67152:0:14:393:397:681:11:g_d0_f10:11:g_d0_f10:C:t
24:835:67153:14:0:393:398:667:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:?:4
24:836:67154:0:24:526:540:674:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:A:(6)
24:837:67157:24:17:88:540:650:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:A:Subtracting theSW(θ∗f) as written in Equation (5), we have the welfare gains of a standard
24:838:67247:17:32:72:237:633:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:relative to the market equilibrium:
24:839:67282:32:25:123:540:601:11:g_d0_f10:11:g_d0_f3:A:SWstandard−SW(θ∗f) =λ(1−θ∗f)2(GHE−GI) + (1−λ)(GLE−GI) +αθ∗2f(7)
24:840:67345:25:16:88:539:576:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:A:The first term is gains to the share of High types that are uninformed in the market equilibrium.
24:841:67442:16:17:71:539:560:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:The second term is negative, capturing losses from Low types who must now purchase goodE.  The
24:842:67536:17:16:71:539:543:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:third term is savings in information provision costs.  Welfare gains are mechanically larger when
24:843:67633:16:17:71:540:527:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:the social gains from goodEare larger and when there are more High types.  Welfare gains are
24:844:67725:17:31:71:405:510:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:also larger whenαis large, i.e.  when it is costly to inform consumers.
24:845:67796:31:24:71:423:479:11:g_d0_f12:11:g_d0_f12:C:4.4.2    Welfare Effects of Government-Provided Sales Incentives
24:846:67860:24:16:71:539:455:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:Unlike minimum quality standards, it would be novel for governments to provide sales incentives
24:847:67955:16:17:71:539:439:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:directly to sales agents.  What effects would this have in this model?  Consider the case where firms
24:848:68056:17:16:71:539:422:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:under-provide information relative to the social optimum (i.e.θ+> θ∗), so the government would
24:849:68150:16:16:71:539:406:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:like to subsidize information provision.  Assume that the government can fund the subsidy with
24:850:68244:16:17:71:150:390:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:lump-sum taxes.
24:851:68259:17:16:88:540:373:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:A:If firms can sets <0 (or provide a higher sales incentive for goodI), then government-provided
24:852:68353:16:17:71:539:357:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:sales incentives act just like a marginal cost reduction, and firms will offset the government incentive
24:853:68457:17:16:71:539:340:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:to  arrive  at  their  profit  maximizing  level  of  information  provision  in  Equation  (18).   However,
24:854:68565:16:17:71:539:324:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:consider the potentially-realistic case where the firm cannot sets <0, i.e.  it cannot pay its agents
24:855:68666:17:16:71:539:307:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:tonotsell  a  product  or  otherwise  undo  the  government-provided  sales  incentive.   In  this  case,
24:856:68771:16:16:71:539:291:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:the government will set the sales incentive that induces the socially-optimal information provision
24:857:68870:16:17:71:539:275:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:effort, and the firm will provide no additional sales incentive and will adjust the fixed wage such
24:858:68969:17:16:71:540:258:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:that agents’ participation constraint binds.  Substitutingθ+into the agents’ first-order condition in
24:859:69070:16:33:71:536:242:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:Equation (2) and simplifying, this gives the socially-optimal government-provided sales incentive:
24:860:69168:33:0:265:288:209:11:g_d0_f10:11:g_d0_f3:?:s+=
24:861:69171:0:15:309:329:216:11:g_d0_f10:8:g_d0_f4:?:αθ+
24:862:69174:15:0:292:345:201:11:g_d0_f10:11:g_d0_f3:?:λ(1−12θ+)
24:863:69183:0:29:526:540:209:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:A:(8)
24:864:69186:29:16:88:539:180:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:A:Increased information provision also has the side effect of increasing competition in the market
24:865:69282:16:17:71:540:164:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:for goodE, so both firms decrease their pricesp∗fE.  In this model, this has no welfare implications,
24:866:69383:17:0:71:338:147:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:but it does generate a transfer from firms to consumers.
25:867:69441:0:24:72:164:691:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:C:4.5    Discussion
25:868:69458:24:16:72:540:667:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:The model helps to understand and motivate the field experiment that we detail in the remainder
25:869:69553:16:17:72:540:651:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:of the paper.  The three simple propositions show that sales agent behavior is not only important
25:870:69650:17:16:72:540:634:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:in  directly  determining  the  firm’s  ability  to  disclose  information,  but  also  indirectly  informative
25:871:69761:16:17:72:540:618:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:about consumers’ preferences:  because information provision is costly, optimizing agents will not
25:872:69859:17:16:72:540:601:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:inform  consumers  if  they  believe  that  information  will  not  affect  demand.   The  social  welfare
25:873:69965:16:17:72:540:585:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:discussion highlights that if sellers’ information disclosure is not effective at increasing demand for
25:874:70068:17:16:72:539:568:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:high quality goods but the social benefit of allocating goodEto High types (GHE−GI) is large,
25:875:70161:16:16:71:539:552:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:minimum quality (energy efficiency) standards are more likely to increase welfare.  Before drawing
25:876:70259:16:17:71:539:536:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:this conclusion, however, we would need to show that information provision is ineffective because
25:877:70356:17:16:71:539:519:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:disclosure is difficult (i.e.αis large), not because consumers still don’t want goodEafter being
25:878:70452:16:17:71:539:503:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:informed (i.e.λis small).  The model also highlights a novel policy that could increase welfare:
25:879:70548:17:16:71:539:486:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:government-provided sales incentives.  To evaluate this potential policy, one similarly needs to know
25:880:70649:16:38:71:232:470:11:g_d0_f10:11:g_d0_f3:B:αandλ, along with (GHE−GI).
25:881:70676:38:28:71:235:432:14:g_d0_f2:14:g_d0_f2:C:5    Experiment Results
25:882:70699:28:24:71:228:404:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:C:5.1    Sales Agent Behavior
25:883:70726:24:16:71:540:380:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:DefineNiatas a measure of whether agentaprovides information to consumeriduring phasetof
25:884:70814:16:16:72:539:364:11:g_d0_f3:8:g_d0_f11:B:the experiment.  We observe sales agent behavior from two sources:  self-reported complianceNsiat
25:885:70911:16:17:72:540:348:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:and the independent audits.  While the latter measure is only available for a smaller subset of calls,
25:886:71013:17:16:72:540:331:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:it is an independent assessment and also provides multiple measures of what the sales agent said.
25:887:71110:16:17:72:539:315:11:g_d0_f12:8:g_d0_f11:F:Tiis a vector of indicator variables for each of the eight treatment cells.  We estimate howNiat
25:888:71206:17:16:72:539:298:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:varies across treatments using the following equation, whereφtis a vector of indicators for the four
25:889:71306:16:30:72:450:282:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:phases of the experiment,μais an agent fixed effect, andυiatis the error term:
25:890:71384:30:30:240:540:252:11:g_d0_f10:11:g_d0_f3:A:Niat=βTi+φt+μa+υiat(9)
25:891:71406:30:16:88:540:222:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:A:Theφtandμacontrols are necessary because assignment probabilities vary across phases as we
25:892:71496:16:16:72:540:206:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:added treatment groups and across agents who were assigned to Information Treatment or Control.
25:893:71591:16:17:72:540:190:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:This equation is estimated as a linear probability model (LPM) in OLS with robust standard errors.
25:894:71689:17:16:72:540:173:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:In typical cases like ours where the true probability model is not known, Angrist and Pischke (2012)
25:895:71789:16:17:72:540:157:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:advocate for using the LPM instead of an arbitrary non-linear model such as probit or logit, and
25:896:71885:17:16:72:540:140:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:we follow their recommendation.  In practice, our results are qualitatively and quantitatively very
25:897:71984:16:17:72:288:124:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:similar when using probit, logit, or the LPM.
25:898:72029:17:16:88:540:107:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:A:Column 1 of Table 4 presents the results using self-reported complianceNsiatas the measure
25:899:72119:16:0:72:540:91:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:of compliance.  The sample excludes the spiff treatment calls because agents were not explicitly
26:900:72217:0:17:72:540:691:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:asked to read a script on these calls.  Agents report that they read the script on 46 to 49 percent of
26:901:72319:17:16:72:540:674:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:calls, and this depends little on treatment assignment.  Columns 2-7 use data from our independent
26:902:72417:16:17:72:540:658:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:audits, showing that self-reports substantially overstate compliance.  Relative to control group calls,
26:903:72520:17:16:72:540:641:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:agents were about ten percent more likely to mention Energy Star in Information Only treatment

26:911:73218:16:17:72:540:510:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:during the call.  These results are consistent with the results in columns 3, 4, and 5, in that agents
26:912:73320:17:16:72:540:493:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:appear to comply with the experiment protocol on about 15 to 20 percent of calls.  The number of

26:927:74751:31:24:72:305:232:11:g_d0_f12:11:g_d0_f12:C:5.1.1    Measuring Sales Agent Compliance

27:941:75632:17:0:72:137:674:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f10:B:the medianN

27:943:75644:10:13:138:540:671:8:g_d0_f11:11:g_d0_f3:A:ais 11 percent, and one quarter of agents comply more than 40 percent of the time.
27:944:75726:13:17:72:540:658:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:This dispersion implies that we can exploit variation in compliance rates across agents to improve
27:945:75824:17:16:72:540:641:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:power in tests of the effects of information provision on demand.  Using the data in this graph,
27:946:75920:16:17:72:539:625:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:we group agents into four compliance groups withN+a= 0, 0<N+a≤0.2, 0.2<N+a≤0.4, and
27:947:76003:17:0:72:81:608:11:g_d0_f10:11:g_d0_f10:C:N
27:948:76004:0:9:81:88:615:8:g_d0_f4:8:g_d0_f4:?:+
27:949:76005:9:0:81:278:606:8:g_d0_f11:11:g_d0_f10:?:a≥0.4.  We defineGaas the mean ofN
27:950:76039:0:9:279:286:615:8:g_d0_f4:8:g_d0_f4:?:+
27:951:76040:9:14:279:539:606:8:g_d0_f11:11:g_d0_f3:A:aacross all agents within agenta’s compliance group,
27:952:76092:14:17:72:539:592:11:g_d0_f3:8:g_d0_f11:B:where agentais the agent with whom consumerihad his or her final call.  The mean values ofGa
27:953:76184:17:16:71:539:575:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:for agents in the four compliance groups are 0, 0.08, 0.29, and 0.53 respectively.  Agents who were
27:954:76283:16:16:71:540:559:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:audited fewer than five times are automatically assigned theGafor the second compliance group,
27:955:76377:16:32:71:222:543:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:which includes the medianN+a.
27:956:76406:32:24:72:485:511:11:g_d0_f12:11:g_d0_f12:C:5.1.2    Spillovers of Information Provision to Non-Information Group Calls
27:957:76481:24:16:72:540:487:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:One reason why agents might not provide much information about Energy Star is that they might
27:958:76574:16:16:72:540:471:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:not  know  what  to  say,  or  might  not  be  well-practiced  in  discussing  energy  efficiency.   To  test
27:959:76683:16:17:72:540:455:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:whether  agents  learn  to  disclose  information,  we  exploit  the  fact  that  the  experiment  induced
27:960:76789:17:16:72:540:438:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:Information  Treatment  Agents  to  repeatedly  deliver  the  Energy  Star  informational  script,  while
27:961:76894:16:17:72:540:422:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:Information Control Agents were never directly exposed.  We regress the same compliance measures
27:962:76990:17:16:72:540:405:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:from Table 4 on the interaction of Information Treatment Agent indicator variables with a vector
27:963:77086:16:17:72:539:389:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:of treatment group indicators.  DefiningIaas an indicator variable for whether agentais assigned
27:964:77182:17:32:72:329:372:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:as an Information Treatment Agent, the regression is:
27:965:77235:32:25:231:539:340:11:g_d0_f10:11:g_d0_f3:A:Niat=γTiIa+βTi+φt+υiat(10)
27:966:77261:25:16:88:539:315:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:A:Standard errors are clustered by agent.  Table 5 presents the estimatedγcoefficients on the
27:967:77352:16:17:71:539:299:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:interactions ofIawith call treatment assignment indicatorsTi.  The table parallels Table 4, with
27:968:77448:17:16:71:539:282:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:three exceptions.  First, to increase power, we combine the $25 and $100 Rebate groups into one
27:969:77543:16:17:71:539:266:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:indicator.  Second, the samples exclude information treatment calls, because Information Control
27:970:77639:17:16:71:539:249:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:Agents do not have any information treatment calls, and the objective is to compare information
27:971:77734:16:16:71:539:233:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:provision on non-information group calls.  Third, we do not present regressions forPayback Period,
27:972:77832:16:17:71:539:217:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:because agents only quoted payback periods on four audited non-information group calls.  (All four
27:973:77930:17:16:71:267:200:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:involved Information Treatment Agents.)
27:974:77969:16:17:88:539:184:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:A:Table 5 shows that Information Treatment Agents are not more likely than Information Control
27:975:78061:17:16:71:539:167:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:Agents to mention experimental rebates on calls in any treatment group.  Information Treatment
27:976:78155:16:17:71:539:151:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:Agents are, however, more likely to mention Energy Star on control calls and to mention that Energy
27:977:78254:17:16:71:539:134:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:Star saves money on Spiff Only calls.  Column 6 shows that Information Treatment Agents talk
27:978:78346:16:16:71:539:118:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:about Energy Star for approximately 30 percent longer on Spiff Only and control group calls.  The
27:979:78443:16:0:71:539:102:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:standard errors are too wide to determine whether there is a meaningful difference in information
28:980:78542:0:17:72:305:691:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:provision on combination Spiff plus Rebate calls.
28:981:78591:17:16:88:539:674:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:A:These  results  have  two  implications.   First,  they  suggest  that  one  reason  why  the  Retailer’s
28:982:78696:16:17:72:540:658:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:sales agents do not frequently discuss information is that they were not well-practiced at doing so.
28:983:78796:17:16:72:540:641:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:Once Information Treatment Agents learned how to discuss Energy Star on information treatment
28:984:78889:16:17:72:540:625:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:calls, they began to do so without explicit instruction on control and spiff calls.  In the context of
28:985:78991:17:16:72:540:608:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:our model, the experiment reduced the cost of information provisionαfor Information Treatment
28:986:79084:16:17:72:540:592:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:Agents.  Second, these results imply that the estimates of effects of information disclosure on sales
28:987:79185:17:16:72:540:575:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:should take account of spillovers, in the form of increased discussion of energy efficiency on control
28:988:79287:16:32:72:127:559:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:group calls.
28:989:79299:32:24:72:269:527:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:C:5.2    Effects on Consumer Choice
28:990:79332:24:16:72:539:503:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:We examine two binary outcomesYiat: whether the consumer purchases any model from the Retailer
28:991:79426:16:16:72:540:487:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:and  whether  the  consumer  purchases  an  Energy  Star  model.   For  each  outcome,  we  run  three
28:992:79528:16:30:72:431:471:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:specifications.  The first specification is the intent-to-treat (ITT) estimator:
28:993:79608:30:30:242:539:441:11:g_d0_f10:11:g_d0_f3:A:Yiat=τTi+φi+μa+εiat(11)
28:994:79631:30:16:88:381:411:11:g_d0_f3:8:g_d0_f4:A:As above, this includes agent and phase indicator variables.10
28:995:79693:16:17:88:539:395:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:A:The second specification is an instrumental variables (IV) estimator, substituting agent-reported
28:996:79790:17:16:71:540:378:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:complianceNsiatforTiin  Equation  (11)  and  instrumenting  forNsiatwithTi.11This  sample  is
28:997:79883:16:17:71:540:362:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:smaller because it excludes the spiff treatment calls, asNsiatis undefined for these calls.  The third
28:998:79985:17:16:71:539:345:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:specification is what we call the “Scaled ITT” estimate:  we interactTiwithGa, which reflects the
28:999:80082:16:17:71:539:329:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:probability that agentadelivered the specific information or rebate script to consumeri. Intuitively,
28:1000:80183:17:16:71:540:312:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:multiplying by compliance probability scales theτcoefficient to be equivalent to a Local Average
28:1001:80279:16:16:71:205:296:11:g_d0_f3:8:g_d0_f4:B:Treatment Effect (LATE).12
28:1002:80305:16:17:88:539:280:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:A:In this context, the ITT and LATE are likely to bound the average treatment effect of providing
28:1003:80400:17:16:71:539:263:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:information  to  all  consumers.   While  the  ATE  could  theoretically  be  larger  than  the  LATE  if
28:1004:80505:16:17:71:539:247:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:sales agents targeted information at the least responsive consumers, we shall see momentarily that
28:1005:80603:17:16:71:539:230:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:agents appear to target consumers who are more interested in Energy Star.  If all treatment group
28:1006:80700:16:17:71:540:214:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:consumers  withNiat=  0  would  have  had  zero  treatment  effect,  then  the  ITT  equals  the  ATE.
28:1007:80802:17:16:71:539:197:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:On the other hand, if the agents quasi-randomly chose whom to disclose to, then consumers with
28:1008:80896:16:16:71:539:181:11:g_d0_f10:11:g_d0_f3:B:Niat= 0 andNiat= 1 would have the same treatment effect, and the LATE would equal the ATE.
28:1009:80986:16:15:80:539:165:6:g_d0_f5:9:g_d0_f6:F:10Once we control for phases, additional time controls do not improve consistency or efficiency.  Adding month-of-
28:1010:81100:15:11:72:540:150:9:g_d0_f6:9:g_d0_f6:F:sample indicators, for example, does not change coefficients or standard errors.  Furthermore, the estimates do not
28:1011:81215:11:7:72:391:139:9:g_d0_f6:9:g_d0_f6:F:change when we exclude Phase I, which pre-dated the introduction of the spiff.
28:1012:81293:7:11:80:525:132:6:g_d0_f5:9:g_d0_f6:?:11Our previous working paper contained an error in this sentence that incorrectly described our IV procedure.
28:1013:81402:11:15:80:540:121:6:g_d0_f5:9:g_d0_f6:F:12N+iatis  not  statistically  different  across  phases  or  treatment  groups,  so  we  cannot  increase  precision  by  also
28:1014:81529:15:11:72:539:106:9:g_d0_f6:9:g_d0_f6:F:projectingφiorTiontoGia.   AlthoughGiais  a  mean  calculated  with  sampling  error  using  the  audit  data,  we
28:1015:81643:11:0:71:539:95:9:g_d0_f6:9:g_d0_f6:F:calculate that adjusting for sampling error in this generated regressor has only a small impact on the standard errors.
29:1016:81764:0:17:88:539:691:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:A:Table 6 presents the results.  The left three columns show effects on overall sales of any model
29:1017:81860:17:16:72:540:674:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:from the Retailer.  The right three columns show effects on Energy Star sales.  Within each set of
29:1018:81958:16:17:72:540:658:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:three columns, the first is the ITT, the second is the IV using agent-reported compliance, and the
29:1019:82056:17:16:72:540:641:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:third regression is the Scaled ITT. Because the interaction effects between information and the two
29:1020:82155:16:17:72:540:625:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:rebate level are never statistically significant, we drop these terms and report results for six major
29:1021:82257:17:16:72:540:608:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:treatment  groups  relative  to  control.   At  the  bottom  of  the  table,  we  report  the  mean  purchase
29:1022:82366:16:17:72:540:592:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:probabilities in the control group:  about 36 percent of consumers purchase from the Retailer, and
29:1023:82464:17:16:72:378:575:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:about 0.9 percent of consumers purchase an Energy Star model.
29:1024:82525:16:16:88:539:559:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:A:The treatments have no effect on overall sales, except that the ITT and self-report IV suggest
29:1025:82619:16:17:72:540:543:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:that a $25 rebate may reduce purchase probability.  One explanation for this is that even mentioning
29:1026:82719:17:16:72:540:526:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:a small rebate for a different model generates a version of choice overload, complicating the sales
29:1027:82818:16:17:72:540:510:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:interaction and causing a slight decrease in purchase probability.  This would be consistent with
29:1028:82915:17:16:72:540:493:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:other evidence of choice overload, such as Iyengar and Lepper (2000).  Another explanation is that
29:1029:83013:16:17:72:540:477:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:the  result  is  spurious  and  would  not  replicate.   We  find  this  latter  explanation  more  plausible,
29:1030:83123:17:16:72:540:460:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:partially because there is no negative effect in the Scaled ITT. Intuitively, the Scaled ITT differs
29:1031:83223:16:16:72:540:444:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:from the ITT because it weights more heavily the treatment effects from more compliant agents.
29:1032:83317:16:17:72:540:428:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:The fact that the negative association disappears in the Scaled ITT implies that the ITT effect is
29:1033:83415:17:16:72:540:411:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:driven by agents who aren’t actually doing anything to comply with the experiment, which suggests
29:1034:83512:16:17:72:540:395:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:a spurious correlation.  The first two columns of Appendix Table A.2 replicate column 1 for agents
29:1035:83610:17:16:72:540:378:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:in the bottom two vs.  top two compliance groups, confirming that none of the treatments affect
29:1036:83705:16:17:72:305:362:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:sales in the subsample of more compliant agents.
29:1037:83753:17:16:88:539:345:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:A:Although there appears to be little or no effect on the Retailer’s overall sales, columns 4-6 show
29:1038:83851:16:16:72:540:329:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:that the treatments do shift the composition of sales toward Energy Star.  The $100 rebate increases
29:1039:83951:16:17:72:539:313:11:g_d0_f3:8:g_d0_f4:B:Energy Star purchase probability by 0.006 to 0.037 percentage points in the three specifications.13
29:1040:84050:17:16:72:540:296:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:This effect is large against a control group market share of 0.9 percent, although it is small as a share
29:1041:84155:16:17:72:540:280:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:of the total potential market.  The combination of a spiff and $100 rebate has a very large point
29:1042:84252:17:16:72:540:263:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:estimate,  increasing purchase probability by 4 to 22 percentage points.  The standard errors are
29:1043:84349:16:17:72:540:247:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:wide, as this treatment was only offered to a small share of consumers in phase 3 of the experiment.
29:1044:84449:17:16:88:539:230:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:A:The information treatments have a tightly estimated zero statistical effect.  In column 6, the
29:1045:84543:16:17:72:540:214:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:standard  errors  are  tight  enough  to  bound  the  Local  Average  Treatment  Effect  at  less  than  1.5
29:1046:84651:17:16:72:540:197:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:percentage points.  While this would represent a large percent increase in Energy Star purchase
29:1047:84746:16:16:72:508:181:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:probability given the small base, the effect in percentage point terms is economically small.
29:1048:84839:16:17:88:539:165:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:A:Earlier, we documented that although agents effectively never explicitly read a treatment script
29:1049:84935:17:16:72:540:148:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:on a control call, Information Treatment Agents are more likely to mention Energy Star on control
29:1050:85032:16:16:72:540:132:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:calls.  If this increases the probability of Energy Star purchase, then the estimates in Table 6 would
29:1051:85134:16:15:80:539:116:6:g_d0_f5:9:g_d0_f6:F:13In column 4, the combination of the spiff and a $25 rebate appears to reduce demand for Energy Star.  We suspect
29:1052:85248:15:0:72:509:101:9:g_d0_f6:9:g_d0_f6:F:that this result also would not replicate, and it is not statistically significant in the Scaled ITT in column 6.
30:1053:85363:0:17:72:540:691:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:understate  the  true  effects  of  the  information  scripts.   The  audit  data  allow  us  to  address  such
30:1054:85474:17:16:72:540:674:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:spillovers. We construct an alternative “Scaled ITT” estimator, interactingTiwith each compliance
30:1055:85571:16:17:72:539:658:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:group’s average difference inMentioned  E-Starbetween treatment and control calls.  Intuitively,
30:1056:85667:17:16:72:539:641:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:this scales the treatment effect to equal a LATE withMentioned E-Staras the endogenous variable.
30:1057:85763:16:17:72:540:625:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:The third column of Appendix Table A.2 presents the results.  The coefficients and standard errors
30:1058:85861:17:16:72:540:608:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:are  inflated,  as  one  should  expect  from  the  fact  that  the  coefficients  in  Table  4  are  smaller  for
30:1059:85975:16:17:72:540:592:11:g_d0_f7:11:g_d0_f3:B:Mentioned  Energy  Starthan for the variables used to constructGia.  The qualitative results are
30:1060:86071:17:16:71:539:575:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:similar:  the Spiff and $100 Rebate combination still has a very large effect, and the standard errors
30:1061:86173:16:16:71:479:559:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:bound the information effect at no more than 2.7 percent with 90 percent confidence.
30:1062:86257:16:17:88:539:543:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:A:As  discussed  in  Section  2.3,  Energy  Star  models  are  only  substitutable  with  some  standard
30:1063:86359:17:16:71:539:526:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:models. Under the assumption that the treatments do not affect whether or not consumers purchase
30:1064:86455:16:17:71:539:510:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:a substitutable model, we can consistently estimate treatment effects within the sample to the set
30:1065:86553:17:16:71:539:493:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:of  consumers  that  purchase  substitutable  models.   Appendix  Table  A.3  presents  results.   The
30:1066:86655:16:17:71:539:477:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:coefficients are larger than in Table 6, as one should expect from excluding consumers with smaller
30:1067:86754:17:16:71:540:460:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:treatment effects.14The qualitative results are also similar:  the Spiff and $100 Rebate combination
30:1068:86854:16:16:71:539:444:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:has a very large effect, and the standard errors bound the information effect at no more than 4.9
30:1069:86951:16:17:71:539:428:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:percentage points with 90 percent confidence in the “Scaled ITT.” For comparison, Energy Star
30:1070:87044:17:16:71:539:411:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:represents 3.4 percent of substitutable models.  The standard errors suggest that even if sales agents
30:1071:87146:16:17:71:539:395:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:provided information to all callers, Energy Star would still not represent more than 4.9+3.4=8.3
30:1072:87242:17:16:71:539:378:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:percent of the market of substitutable models.  Thus, the lack of seller-provided information does
30:1073:87340:16:17:71:399:362:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:not explain much of the low takeup of energy efficient water heaters.
30:1074:87409:17:16:88:539:345:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:A:Appendix  Table  A.4  presents  alternative  estimates  using  a  probit  estimator;  the  signs  and
30:1075:87510:16:32:71:318:329:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:discrete significance levels are the same or stronger.
30:1076:87564:32:24:71:292:297:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:C:5.3    Targeted Information Disclosure
30:1077:87602:24:16:71:539:273:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:Table 4 documents that the sales agents only partially comply with the experiment.  Are agents
30:1078:87696:16:17:71:539:257:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:strategic in providing information to consumers that are more interested in energy efficiency? Recall
30:1079:87797:17:16:71:539:240:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:thatNsiatis an indicator for whether the consumer is in a treatment group and the agent reported
30:1080:87893:16:16:71:539:224:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:compliance with delivering the script, and defineTias an indicator for whether consumeriis in any
30:1081:87990:16:17:71:539:208:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:rebate or informational treatment group.  We exclude the spiff treatment calls because there was
30:1082:88086:17:16:71:539:191:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:no script for the agent to “comply” with on these calls.  Table 7 reports estimates of the following
30:1083:88186:16:17:71:121:175:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:regression:
30:1084:88197:17:16:195:539:158:11:g_d0_f10:11:g_d0_f3:A:Yiat=ξTiNsiat+κTi(1−Nsiat) +φi+μa+εiat(12)
30:1085:88239:16:15:80:539:142:6:g_d0_f5:9:g_d0_f6:F:14Energy  Star  model  availability  and  consumer  preferences  vary  by  geography,  so  if  geography  were  somehow
30:1086:88358:15:11:72:540:127:9:g_d0_f6:9:g_d0_f6:F:imbalanced across treatment groups, our coefficient estimates would be biased.  Appendix Table A.3 also shows that
30:1087:88472:11:11:72:540:116:9:g_d0_f6:9:g_d0_f6:F:the coefficient estimates are very similar when also including indicators for each purchaser’s three-digit zip code.  Of
30:1088:88592:11:0:72:308:105:9:g_d0_f6:9:g_d0_f6:F:course, this is to be expected in a randomized experiment.
31:1089:88652:0:17:88:539:691:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:A:As outcome variablesYiat, we use two different measures of interest in energy efficiency, both
31:1090:88746:17:16:72:540:674:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:of which could be affected by the treatments.  To construct the dependent variable in column 1,
31:1091:88841:16:17:72:539:658:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f7:B:we exploit an open-answer question from the follow-up survey:What were the two most important
31:1092:88934:17:16:72:540:641:11:g_d0_f7:11:g_d0_f3:B:factors  in  your  water  heater  purchase  decision?The  dependent  variable  is  an  indicator  taking
31:1093:89038:16:17:72:540:625:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:value  one  for  the  consumers  who  had  one  of  their  two  factors  coded  as  “saving  energy  and/or
31:1094:89145:17:16:72:540:608:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:environmental conservation.”  The dependent variable in columns 2-4 is an indicator for whether
31:1095:89240:16:17:72:540:592:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:the consumer purchased Energy Star.  These regressions use agent-reported compliance because the
31:1096:89336:17:16:72:306:575:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:sample of audits is too small for sufficient power.
31:1097:89387:16:16:88:540:559:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:A:The coefficientκmeasures the difference inYiatbetween treatment group consumers who did
31:1098:89474:16:17:72:539:543:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:not receive the treatment and the control group, whileξmeasures the difference between treatment
31:1099:89570:17:16:72:540:526:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:group  consumers  who  did  receive  the  treatment  (according  to  the  agents’  self-reports)  and  the
31:1100:89676:16:17:72:539:510:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:control.ξis a mix of selection effects and treatment effects, whileκis purely selection effects.  If
31:1101:89776:17:16:72:539:493:11:g_d0_f10:11:g_d0_f3:B:κ <0, this implies that the consumers to whom agents are not disclosing information are less likely
31:1102:89875:16:17:72:540:477:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:than average to purchase Energy Star, and thus that consumers who are provided with information
31:1103:89970:17:16:72:540:460:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:are  more  likely  than  average  to  purchase  Energy  Star.   While  this  is  not  the  same  as  targeting
31:1104:90080:16:16:72:540:444:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:information disclosure at consumers who will have the largest treatment effects, it implies targeting
31:1105:90181:16:17:72:251:428:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:in a different and likely related sense.
31:1106:90221:17:16:88:540:411:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:A:In  all  four  columns  of  Table  7,  the  statistically  negative  estimates  ofκshows  that  agents
31:1107:90323:16:17:72:540:395:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:are  more  likely  to  report  delivering  the  script  to  consumers  that  are  more  interested  in  energy
31:1108:90433:17:16:72:540:378:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:efficiency.  Column 3 includes in the sample only consumers who purchase substitutable models.
31:1109:90527:16:17:72:540:362:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:Even within this group, agents still target consumers with a higher probability of purchasing Energy
31:1110:90627:17:16:72:540:345:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:Star.  Column 4 includes controls for the nine address-based demographic variables.  Because these
31:1111:90725:16:16:72:540:329:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:covariates are missing for consumers who did not purchase from the Retailer, the sample is limited
31:1112:90823:16:17:72:540:313:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:to consumers who purchased from the Retailer.  The fact thatκis still negative after conditioning
31:1113:90920:17:16:72:540:296:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:on observables shows that agents target information provision based on other unobservable factors.
31:1114:91018:16:17:88:539:280:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:A:How is such targeting possible?  Based on conversations with sales agents and with our research
31:1115:91113:17:16:72:540:263:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:assistant who carried out the audits, we believe that agents learn about the consumer’s preferences
31:1116:91212:16:17:72:540:247:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:as the call continues.  Agents may have delayed reading the Energy Star script until later in the
31:1117:91309:17:32:72:394:230:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:call, after having the chance to gauge the consumer’s receptiveness.
31:1118:91377:32:23:72:258:198:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:C:5.4    Relationship to the Model
31:1119:91409:23:17:72:540:175:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:Our main empirical results tell a coherent story that is consistent with the three propositions in
31:1120:91507:17:16:72:540:158:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:Section  4.   Proposition  1  states  that  agents  will  not  inform  consumers  if  information  does  not
31:1121:91615:16:17:72:540:142:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:increase demand.  Results in Table 6 and related appendix tables show that information increases
31:1122:91711:17:16:72:540:125:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:Energy  Star  sales  by  at  most  a  few  percentage  points,  even  when  focusing  on  the  Scaled  ITT
31:1123:91817:16:16:72:540:109:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:estimates and limiting the sample only to consumers who are purchasing water heaters that are
31:1124:91910:16:0:72:540:93:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:substitutable  with  Energy  Star  models.   Consistent  with  this  and  with  Proposition  1,  the  audit
32:1125:92019:0:17:72:540:691:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:data show that agents spent very little time discussing Energy Star unless the experiment website
32:1126:92116:17:16:72:540:674:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:directed them to.  Agents mentioned Energy Star on only 13 percent of control group calls, and the
32:1127:92214:16:17:72:459:658:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:median time spent discussing Energy Star within this 13 percent was 15 seconds.
32:1128:92293:17:16:88:539:641:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:A:Proposition 2 states that agents will provide more information when incentivized to do so, but
32:1129:92387:16:17:72:540:625:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:they  will  not  be  very  responsive  to  sales  incentives  if  information  has  small  effects  on  demand.
32:1130:92498:17:16:72:540:608:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:The audit data show that agents provide at best slightly more information about Energy Star on
32:1131:92592:16:17:72:540:592:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:no-rebate spiff calls compared to control:  in Table 4, the coefficient on 1(Spiff Only) is positive but
32:1132:92696:17:16:72:323:575:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:not statistically significant in columns 2, 4, 6, and 7.
32:1133:92752:16:16:88:539:559:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:A:Both of Propositions 1 and 2 illustrate the interaction between the supply and demand sides
32:1134:92843:16:17:72:540:543:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:of  the  market.   It  was  difficult  for  the  Retailer  to  increase  information  provision  through  the
32:1135:92952:17:16:72:540:526:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:experiment  because  their  sales  agents  knew  that  most  consumers  would  be  unresponsive  to  the
32:1136:93056:16:17:72:540:510:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:information.   The  small  Local  Average  Treatment  Effects  in  the  IV  and  Scaled  ITT  estimators,
32:1137:93161:17:16:72:540:493:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:combined  with  the  targeting  results  in  Table  7,  suggest  that  agents’  lack  of  compliance  is  best
32:1138:93271:16:17:72:540:477:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:characterized as “strategic,”  not “shirking.”  In the context of the model,  we mean that agents’
32:1139:93369:17:16:72:540:460:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:information disclosure costαis low enough that if more consumers were “High types” that would
32:1140:93462:16:16:72:540:444:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:potentially be interested in Energy Star, agents might devote more effort to marketing those models.
32:1141:93562:16:17:88:539:428:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:A:Proposition 3 states that sales incentives and customer rebates reinforce each other, because the
32:1142:93659:17:16:72:540:411:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:rebate increases sales agents’ gains from responding to the sales incentive.  Although the standard
32:1143:93758:16:17:72:540:395:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:errors are wide, the point estimates in the sales data in Table 6 strongly support this: the combined
32:1144:93859:17:16:72:540:378:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:Spiff and $100 rebate treatment substantially increases Energy Star purchase probability. The audit
32:1145:93958:16:17:72:540:362:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:data provide evidence that is suggestive of the microfoundations for this result.  Specifically, agents
32:1146:94061:17:16:72:540:345:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:appear to be slightly more likely to market Energy Star on the spiff treatment calls as the rebates
32:1147:94160:16:16:72:540:329:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:increase from $0 to $25 to $100:  in Table 6, the point estimates in columns 2, 3, 4, 6, and 7 all
32:1148:94258:16:17:72:224:313:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:increase as the rebates increase.
32:1149:94291:17:16:88:539:296:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:A:Finally,  the  model  considers  a  potential  role  for  government-provided  sales  incentives,  which
32:1150:94395:16:17:72:540:280:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:could perhaps be a complement to product subsidies traditionally offered by governments and util-
32:1151:94492:17:16:72:540:263:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:ity energy efficiency programs.  The empirical results in Table 6 suggest a strong complementarity
32:1152:94590:16:17:72:540:247:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:between price reductions and sales incentives.  The model clarifies that government-provided in-
32:1153:94686:17:16:72:540:230:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:centives could increase welfare in the presence of an informational market failure, as long as firms
32:1154:94786:16:17:72:540:214:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:are  not  able  to  fully  “undo”  the  government  incentive  by  changing  their  agents’  compensation
32:1155:94891:17:32:72:118:197:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:structure.
32:1156:94901:32:23:72:330:165:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:C:5.5    Why Is Demand for Energy Star Low?
32:1157:94942:23:17:72:540:142:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:Equation (7) shows that a minimum energy efficiency standard is more likely to increase welfare if
32:1158:95040:17:16:72:540:125:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:the energy efficient product generates utility gains for a larger share of the population or if the cost
32:1159:95144:16:16:72:540:109:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:of providing information is high.  Our results show that the experimental attempts at information
32:1160:95241:16:0:72:540:93:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:provision do not significantly increase Energy Star demand. Does this suggest that minimum energy
33:1161:95340:0:17:72:456:691:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:efficiency standards might increase welfare by addressing imperfect information?
33:1162:95420:17:16:88:539:674:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:A:A first potential explanation for our empirical results is that although the Energy Star product
33:1163:95516:16:17:72:540:658:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:would generate gains for many consumers, the Retailer is not able to credibly inform consumers
33:1164:95610:17:16:72:540:641:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:of this, perhaps due to time constraints on the sales interactions or an inability to credibly convey
33:1165:95711:16:17:72:540:625:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:attributes of this higher-priced product.  If this were true, many consumers would remain unaware
33:1166:95808:17:16:72:540:608:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:of  Energy  Star  and  unconvinced  of  the  cost  savings.   A  second  explanation  is  that  the  Energy
33:1167:95915:16:17:72:540:592:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:Star model would not in fact generate utility gains for many consumers, and consumers make an
33:1168:96008:17:16:72:540:575:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:informed decision to not purchase the product.  If this were true, consumers would be aware of the
33:1169:96106:16:16:72:355:559:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:Energy Star product and the potential energy cost savings.
33:1170:96164:16:17:88:539:543:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:A:We use results from the follow-up surveys to measure the importance of these two explanations.
33:1171:96258:17:16:72:540:526:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f7:B:Near the end of the survey,  we asked consumers,Some  water  heater  models  that  use  less  energy
33:1172:96358:16:17:71:539:510:11:g_d0_f7:11:g_d0_f3:B:are officially designated as Energy Star.  Did you buy an Energy Star model?The results suggest
33:1173:96453:17:16:71:539:493:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:substantial confusion, consistent with the first explanation.  The top panel of Table 8 shows that
33:1174:96551:16:17:71:539:477:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:while only 2.1 percent actually purchased Energy Star, 52 percent of survey respondents think that
33:1175:96649:17:16:71:539:460:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:they did.  This should be interpreted cautiously,  as there could have been experimenter demand
33:1176:96744:16:16:71:539:444:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:effects:  respondents may not have wanted to tell the interviewer that they had not purchased the
33:1177:96841:16:17:71:539:428:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:Energy Star option.  We designed the survey specifically to reduce demand effects:  this was the
33:1178:96937:17:16:71:539:411:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:first question we asked about energy efficiency, and we asked it after a series of other questions that
33:1179:97040:16:17:71:407:395:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:signaled that the interviewer was not particularly interested in energy.
33:1180:97112:17:16:88:539:378:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:A:Respondents who said they had not purchased Energy Star,  or who were ”Not Sure” but in
33:1181:97199:16:17:71:539:362:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:fact had not,  were asked why they had not purchased Energy Star.  The bottom panel of Table
33:1182:97291:17:16:71:539:345:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:8 shows that the primary reason was high prices.  This is consistent with the second explanation
33:1183:97387:16:16:71:539:329:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:of informed consumers choosing not to purchase Energy Star.  Fifteen percent of these consumers
33:1184:97482:16:17:71:539:313:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:(or about seven percent of the entire surveyed population) report being unaware that there was an
33:1185:97579:17:16:71:165:296:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:Energy Star option.
33:1186:97598:16:17:88:539:280:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:A:The  follow-up  survey  also  elicited  beliefs  over  energy  costs  for  standard  models  and  energy
33:1187:97702:17:16:71:539:263:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:cost  savings  from  Energy  Star  models.   Table  9  shows  the  10th,  50th,  and  90th  percentiles  of
33:1188:97809:16:17:71:539:247:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:beliefs, along with the mean and the best estimate of the true value, from the yellow tags.  The
33:1189:97905:17:16:71:539:230:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:first question in Table 9 shows that consumers’ mean beliefs about water heater energy costs are
33:1190:98001:16:17:71:539:214:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:approximately in line with the yellow tags.  The second question, however, suggests that the mean
33:1191:98098:17:16:71:539:197:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:and  median  consumers  actually  overestimate  the  average  dollar  value  of  potential  cost  savings.
33:1192:98204:16:16:71:539:181:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:The third question takes the ratio of the second question to the first, which translates to a percent
33:1193:98305:16:17:71:539:165:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:savings and can account for heterogeneity in consumers’ utilization.  The “true” mean energy cost
33:1194:98402:17:16:71:539:148:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:savings  on  the  yellow  tags  are  about  10  percent,  while  the  median  and  mean  consumers  report
33:1195:98508:16:16:71:539:132:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:believing  that  Energy  Star  could  save  25  and  32  percent,  respectively.15Of  course,  the  beliefs
33:1196:98615:16:15:80:539:116:6:g_d0_f5:9:g_d0_f6:F:15Additional (unreported) regressions show that confusion about Energy Star purchases and beliefs about Energy
33:1197:98725:15:0:72:410:101:9:g_d0_f6:9:g_d0_f6:F:Star savings do not vary across treatment groups, although estimates are imprecise.
34:1198:98810:0:17:72:540:691:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:were elicited in a phone survey and not made incentive compatible, so they should be interpreted
34:1199:98906:17:16:72:540:674:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:cautiously.  Notwithstanding, they suggest that underestimating energy cost savings is not a barrier
34:1200:99006:16:39:72:182:658:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:to Energy Star takeup.
34:1201:99028:39:27:72:173:619:14:g_d0_f2:14:g_d0_f2:C:6    Conclusion
34:1202:99043:27:16:72:540:592:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:Imperfect information is an oft-cited reason why regulators intervene in markets for energy-using
34:1203:99140:16:17:72:540:576:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:durables though mandatory information disclosure, subsidies, and standards.  In theory, one natural
34:1204:99239:17:16:72:540:559:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:way  for  consumers  to  learn  about  the  benefits  of  energy  efficient  products  is  through  retailers.
34:1205:99349:16:16:72:540:543:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:Motivated by this, we partnered with a large nationwide retailer to test the effects of information
34:1206:99448:16:17:72:540:527:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:provision, customer rebates, and sales incentives on the behavior of both sales agents and consumers.
34:1207:99549:17:16:72:539:510:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:We also present a simple model which, while not a theoretical advanceper  se, helps to motivate
34:1208:99644:16:17:72:255:494:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:the experiment and clarify the results.
34:1209:99683:17:16:88:539:477:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:A:Results show that retailer-provided information is ineffective at increasing Energy Star demand,
34:1210:99779:16:17:72:540:461:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:even after adjusting for partial compliance by sales agents.  Knowing that information would be
34:1211:99874:17:16:72:540:444:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:ineffective, sales agents appear to have marketed Energy Star to only the most receptive consumers,
34:1212:99973:16:17:72:540:428:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:strategically failing to provide information to the majority. Follow-up surveys provide some evidence
34:1213:100074:17:16:72:540:411:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:that at least some consumers who bought from the Retailer are unaware of the Energy Star product
34:1214:100170:16:16:72:540:395:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:or  confused  about  what  they  have  bought.   The  majority  of  consumers  who  bought  from  the
34:1215:100271:16:17:72:540:379:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:Retailer and completed our survey, however, are aware of Energy Star and may even overestimate
34:1216:100365:17:16:72:540:362:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:its benefits.  These results highlight the difficulties that retailers can face in increasing demand for
34:1217:100469:16:17:72:540:346:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:energy efficient or otherwise “high-quality” products.  In this context, a key difficulty appears to
34:1218:100569:17:16:72:540:329:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:be that many consumers still don’t view energy efficiency as a privately-beneficial investment, even
34:1219:100669:16:17:72:283:313:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:after the retailer’s attempts to inform them.
34:1220:100714:17:16:88:539:296:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:A:The water heater market has some unusual features,  and our sample comprises only a small
34:1221:100803:16:16:72:540:280:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:share of that market.  What broader lessons can be drawn from our results?  First, our results fit
34:1222:100901:16:17:72:540:264:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:into a broader set of results from the literature suggesting that while social comparisons or various
34:1223:101002:17:16:72:540:247:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:forms of persuasion can motivate pro-environmental behaviors, hard information about energy costs
34:1224:101099:16:17:72:540:231:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:seems to have more limited effects.  As our model makes clear, “hard” information about product
34:1225:101194:17:16:72:540:214:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:availability  (as  well  as  product  costs  and  benefits)  is  more  relevant  from  a  welfare  perspective
34:1226:101304:16:17:72:540:198:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:because  a  regulator’s  inability  to  address  imperfect  information  could  justify  corrective  policies,
34:1227:101414:17:16:72:540:181:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:while the welfare implications of persuasion are less clear.  Our experimental design does not allow
34:1228:101514:16:17:72:540:165:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:us to cleanly distinguish whether consumers are more generally uninformed or whether they are
34:1229:101607:17:16:72:540:148:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:simply disinterested in information from the retailer’s agents.  Notwithstanding, our survey results
34:1230:101707:16:16:72:540:132:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:help  somewhat  to  resolve  this  question.   Furthermore,  the  water  heater  market  is  certainly  one
34:1231:101814:16:17:72:540:116:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:where consumers begin the process with very little information and do rely on agents’ knowledge
34:1232:101909:17:0:72:261:99:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:for many other aspects of the purchase.
35:1233:101950:0:17:88:539:691:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:A:Second,  our  theoretical  and  empirical  results  clearly  suggest  that  policymakers  interested  in
35:1234:102054:17:16:72:540:674:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:maximizing the effects of subsidy dollars on Energy Star purchases might consider allocating some
35:1235:102151:16:17:72:540:658:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:incentives to sales agents, not just to consumers.  While the magnitude of our effect size is certainly
35:1236:102254:17:16:72:540:641:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:specific to our context, this general suggestion is novel. Third, our results provide unusually granular
35:1237:102358:16:17:72:540:625:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:insight into the role of sales agents in the process of information disclosure.  In many situations
35:1238:102457:17:16:72:540:608:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:like ours, a firm or policymaker must consider how to incentivize agents if they want to increase
35:1239:102554:16:17:72:540:592:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:information disclosure.  In equilibrium, firms and policymakers can also potentially learn about the
35:1240:102654:17:0:72:455:575:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:value of information from whether experienced sales agents choose to provide it.
